============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO5)
============================================================
GT: -beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5 - omega0**c6*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is
\[
F(x,v)= -0.8961236228\,v\;-\;0.4480618114\sin(v)\;-\;1.2939539026\,x^3\;-\;1.2939539026\,x\,(0.09430567863|v|^{1/3}+1)\;-\;1.2939539026\,x.
\]
So GT contains these *essential* structures:

- a **sin(v)** term with nonzero coefficient;
- a **linear v** term;
- an **x·|v|^{1/3}** term (fractional power of |v| multiplied by x);
- polynomial-in-x terms: **x³** and **x** (indeed two x-linear contributions combine to \(-2.5879...x\), but still just linear in x).

Any candidate must be able (possibly under a plausible domain restriction like \(v\ge 0\) or \(x\ge 0\)) to reproduce **sin(v)** and **x|v|^{1/3}**. None of the candidates include \(|v|^{1/3}\) (they have \(v|v|\), \(v|v|^3\), logs, exp, etc.), and none include \(\sin(v)\) (some have \(\sin(\text{affine in }t)\) or \(\sin(\text{affine in }x)\), which cannot equal \(\sin(v)\) as a function of independent variables). Domain restrictions like \(v\ge 0\) can turn \(|v|\) into \(v\), but cannot turn integer powers into \(v^{1/3}\), nor can they convert \(\sin(x)\) or \(\sin(t)\) into \(\sin(v)\).

Below I check each candidate against these required GT components.

---

Polynomial in \(x\), \(v\), plus \(v|v|\), \(v^3\), Max(0,x)^3, \(x^5\).  
Missing **sin(v)** and missing **x|v|^{1/3}** ⇒ cannot match.

GT: -beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*(gamma*Abs(v)**c2 + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5 - omega0**c6*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
`-0.896123622766678*v - 1.29395390256765*x**3 - 1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.29395390256765*x - 0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

Let me simplify:
- `-0.896123622766678*v` (linear in v)
- `-1.29395390256765*x**3` (cubic in x)
- `-1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1)` = `-0.122048*x*Abs(v)**0.333333 - 1.29395390256765*x`
- `-1.29395390256765*x` (linear in x)
- `-0.448061811383339*sin(v)` (sine of v)

Combining the x terms: `-1.29395390256765*x - 1.29395390256765*x = -2.58790780513530*x`

So GT = `-1.29395390256765*x**3 - 2.58790780513530*x - 0.122048*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 0.896123622766678*v - 0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `x**3`
2. `x`
3. `x*|v|^(1/3)`
4. `v`
5. `sin(v)`

This is critical: the GT contains `sin(v)` and `x*|v|^(1/3)`. These are very specific basis functions.

Now let me check each candidate. For a candidate to match, it must be able to reproduce ALL five basis functions exactly. Since candidate constants are free, I need to check if the candidate's functional form can express these terms.

**Key observations:**
- `sin(v)` is required - no polynomial in v can reproduce this
- `x*|v|^(1/3)` is required - this is a very unusual term

Let me quickly scan all candidates for `sin(v)`:

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)`. They contain `sin(t)`, `sin(x)`, `cos(t)`, but NOT `sin(v)`.

Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, and other basis functions present in the candidates, NO candidate can exactly reproduce the GT.

Wait - let me reconsider. Could `sin(v)` be approximated by some combination? No - Rule 2 strictly forbids approximations. `sin(v)` is linearly independent from polynomials in v (like `v`, `v**3`, `v*|v|`, etc.) and from exponentials.

Also, `x*|v|^(1/3)` is not present in any candidate either.

Let me verify each candidate systematically, but the absence of `sin(v)` in ALL candidates means none can match.

Going through all 50 candidates: None contain `sin(v)` as a basis function. The closest terms involving trigonometric functions of v don't exist. Some have `sin(t)`, `sin(x)`, `cos(t)`, but never `sin(v)`.

Since `sin(v)` with a non-zero coefficient (-0.448...) is part of the GT, and `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all other basis functions (polynomials, exponentials, logs, etc.), no candidate can match.
